diagnose_training_tracks_issue

  • Show All Code
  • Hide All Code
Author

Saideep Gona

Published

September 20, 2023

Context

I recently have been performing training of the Enformer prediction to Aracena track models. While the training appears to be occuring, with convergence of the loss function, etc. The output predictions appear nonsensical. After visual inspection, it seems that some of the tracks donâ€™t really match expectations. For example, RNAseq coverage should line up with gene annotations. Here I am going to try and find the source of the discrepancy.

Enformer predictions (model inputs)

These appear to match up with the expected (similar to Enformer usage notebook)

Aracena tracks

By visual inspection, there is likely a problem with the Aracena tracks not aligning with the expected region. Because this data is very important, I am going to create some checks and utility code from the ground up.

Aracena BAM files

Since the BAM files are aligned to hg19, I will start by extracting RNAseq coverage from a gene region in hg19 coordinates, followed by repeating with liftover coordinates. This coverage should align with expectations assuming the bam files are correct.

Code 
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sns
import numpy as np

def plot_tracks(tracks, interval, height=1.5):
  fig, axes = plt.subplots(len(tracks), 1, figsize=(20, height * len(tracks)), sharex=True)
  for ax, (title, y) in zip(axes, tracks.items()):
    ax.fill_between(np.linspace(interval[1], interval[2], num=len(y)), y)
    ax.set_title(title)
    sns.despine(top=True, right=True, bottom=True)
  ax.set_xlabel("_".join([str(x) for x in interval]))
  plt.tight_layout()
Code 
ERAP2_window_hg19 = ["5",96211643,96255420] 
ERAP2_window_hg38 = ["5",96875939,96919716]

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import numpy as np

bam_file = "/project2/haky/saideep/aracena_data_preprocessing/RNAseq_alignment/AF20_NI.sorted.mdup.bam"

with pysam.AlignmentFile(bam_file, "rb") as rnaseq_ara_bam:
    ERAP2_hg19_cov = rnaseq_ara_bam.count_coverage(*ERAP2_window_hg19)

Ok lets check that lifting over the coordinates works as expected

Code 
import kipoiseq

def liftover_coords(interval, source="hg19", target="hg38"):
    '''
    Inputs:
        interval: kipoiseq interval object containing the coordinates to be converted
    Outputs:
        converted_coords: kipoiseq interval object containing the converted coordinates
    '''
    import liftover
    # Initialize converter

    converter = liftover.get_lifter(source, target)

    converted_coords = kipoiseq.Interval(interval.chrom,converter[interval.chrom][interval.start][0][1],converter[interval.chrom][interval.end][0][1])

    return converted_coords

ERAP2_hg19_kipoi = kipoiseq.Interval("chr5",96211643,96255420)

ERAP2_hg38_kipoi = kipoiseq.Interval("chr5",96875939,96919716)

ERAP2_hg38_from_hg19 = liftover_coords(ERAP2_hg19_kipoi)

ERAP2_hg19_from_hg38 = liftover_coords(ERAP2_hg38_kipoi, source="hg38", target="hg19")

print("ERAP2 hg38 window ground truth:",ERAP2_hg38_kipoi)
print("ERAP2 hg38 window from liftover hg19:",ERAP2_hg38_from_hg19)
print("ERAP2 hg19 window ground truth:",ERAP2_hg19_kipoi)
print("ERAP2 hg19 window from liftover hg38:",ERAP2_hg19_from_hg38)

The liftover is working. It turns out that a possible source of error is that I was performing liftover in the wrong direction. Since the basenji sequences are mapped to hg38, and the aracena alignments are mapped to hg19, I need to perform liftover from hg38 to hg19 to get the extraction coordinates. In my liftover function, however, it defaults to hg19 to hg38. Letâ€™s continue testing the conversion process by looking at the bigwigs.

def update_target_array_single_bin(bigwig_files, coords, summarization="mean", bin_size=128):

    # Iterate through coords and extract targets
    bw_array = np.zeros((1,len(bigwig_files)))
    for i,bw in enumerate(bigwig_files):
        if "RNAseq" in bw:
            cur_chrom = coords.chrom.replace("chr","")
        else:
            cur_chrom = coords.chrom
        # Initialize reader
        try:
            with pyBigWig.open(bw) as reader:
                
                try:
                    cur_val = reader.stats(cur_chrom, coords.start, coords.end, type=summarization)
                    # print("Read from bigwig file: "+bw, coords)
                    # print(cur_val)
                except Exception as e:
                    print("Error reading bigwig file: "+bw, coords)
                    print(e)
                    cur_val = [0]
            
                bw_array[0,i] = cur_val[0]
        except Exception as e:
            print("Error opening bigwig file: "+bw, coords)
            print(e)

    # print("shape of bw array: ", bw_array.shape)

    return bin_size*bw_array

def extract_targets_single_window(bigwig_files, coords, summarization="mean", bin_size=128, bin_count=896, num_cpus=2):

    import multiprocessing as mp

    # Target matrix is output bins x num tracks x num windows

    target_array = np.zeros((896,12))

    # Iterate through coords and extract targets

    bin_coords = np.arange(coords.start, coords.end, 128)

    bin_update_params = []

    for i,coord in enumerate(bin_coords):

        bin_update_params.append((bigwig_files,kipoiseq.Interval(coords.chrom,coord,coord+bin_size)))
        # print(bin_update_params)
    
    with mp.Pool(num_cpus) as pool:
        bin_arrays = pool.starmap(update_target_array_single_bin, bin_update_params)

    target_array = np.concatenate(bin_arrays, axis=0)
    print("shape of target array: ", target_array.shape)

    return target_array

import h5py

def query_epigenome_from_hdf5(region, individual="AF20"):
    import pandas as pd
    import h5py 

    col_region = "_".join([region[0].strip("chr"),region[1],region[2]])

    mapping_table = pd.read_csv("/beagle3/haky/users/saideep/projects/aracena_modeling/hdf5_training/index_files/remapped_table_filt.csv", index_col=0)

    if col_region not in mapping_table.columns:
        print(col_region, "not present in hdf5")
        return None,"region not present in hdf5"

    query_index = int(mapping_table.loc["ref-epigenome", col_region])
    query_group = mapping_table.loc["group", col_region]

    print(query_index,query_group)

    enformer_ref_targets = f"/beagle3/haky/users/saideep/projects/aracena_modeling/hdf5_training/ref-epigenome_{query_group}_aracena.h5"

    with h5py.File(enformer_ref_targets, 'r') as ert:
        query = ert['ref_epigenome'][:,4766,query_index]

    return query, None


def query_aracena_from_hdf5(region, individual="AF20"):
    import pandas as pd
    import h5py 

    col_region = "_".join([region[0].strip("chr"),region[1],region[2]])

    mapping_table = pd.read_csv("/beagle3/haky/users/saideep/projects/aracena_modeling/hdf5_training/index_files/remapped_table_filt.csv", index_col=0)

    if col_region not in mapping_table.columns:
        print(col_region, "not present in hdf5")
        return None,"region not present in hdf5"

    query_index = int(mapping_table.loc[individual, col_region])
    query_group = mapping_table.loc["group", col_region]

    print(query_index,query_group)

    enformer_ara_targets = f"/beagle3/haky/users/saideep/projects/aracena_modeling/hdf5_training/{individual}_{query_group}_aracena.h5"
    print(enformer_ara_targets)
    with h5py.File(enformer_ara_targets, 'r') as ert:
        query = ert['targets'][:,0,query_index]

    return query, None


def query_epigenome(chr_num, center_bp, enfref_dir, num_bins=896, tracks=-1):
    """
    Parameters:
        path_to_enfref (str): path to the directory containing the concatenated reference enformer files
        chr_num (int/string): chromosome number
        center_bp (int): center base pair position (1-indexed)
        num_bins (int): number of bins to extract centered around center_bp (default: 896) 
            note: if the number of bins is even, the center bin will be in the second half of the array
        tracks (int list): list of tracks to extract (default: all 5313 tracks)

    Returns:
        epigen (np.array): enformer predictions centered at center_bp of shape (num_bins, len(tracks))
    """

    # from position choose center bin
    center_ind = center_bp - 1
    center_bin = center_ind // 128
    
    half_bins = num_bins // 2
    start_bin = center_bin - half_bins
    end_bin = center_bin + half_bins
    if num_bins % 2 != 0: # if num_bins is odd
        end_bin += 1

    with h5py.File(f"{enfref_dir}/chr{chr_num}_cat.h5", "r") as f:
        # get tracks if list provided
        if tracks == -1:
            epigen = f[f'chr{chr_num}'][start_bin:end_bin, :] 
        else:
            epigen = f[f'chr{chr_num}'][start_bin:end_bin, tracks] 

    return epigen

I can now make a function which calculates the tss bin for a given basenji region/interval

Code 
def calc_tss_bins(region, tss_list, bin_size = 128):
    region_start = int(region.split("_")[1])
    tss_bins = set()
    for tss in tss_list:
        tss_dif = tss - region_start
        tss_bins.add(tss_dif//bin_size)
    return tss_bins


def plot_tracks(tracks, interval, vlines,height=1.5):

  fig, axes = plt.subplots(len(tracks), 1, figsize=(20, height * len(tracks)), sharex=True)

  for ax, (title, y) in zip(axes, tracks.items()):
    ax.fill_between(np.linspace(interval[1], interval[2], num=len(y)), y)
    ax.set_title(title, fontsize=18)
    ax.vlines(list(vlines),0, max(y), color="red")
    sns.despine(top=True, right=True, bottom=True)

  ax.set_xlabel("_".join([str(x) for x in interval]))
  plt.tight_layout()
